5.3.3 Connection Medallion  
The necklace serves as a token or relic to one. We wanted to give something personal to every member 
to feel united and special. In the ideation sessions we designed different versions of this product, 
bracelet, business card, hangtag. We chose to present the necklace because it resonates us the most. 
Idea in: The Connection Medallion is a smart gadget that uses a near-field communication (NFC) chip. 
The chip is built within the necklace’s spiky crystal part (the main body) and carries the identification 
information of every member. This technology is already available today in the event industry 
(EVENTMB STUDIO TEAM, 2017). The crystal itself is unique for each member, as every crystal has 
crystals of different lengths. This makes the necklace both a digital and physical identification mark. 
The physical identification item can be inserted into any console in Heterotopia. One of these consoles 
is in the Transparency room. The console has a grid structure keyhole that works the same way as keys 
work – they press down the cubical pins at different heights. 
Idea with: Every member has a connection medallion. It carries a lot of value and usefulness in an 
Heterotopian's life. First and foremost, it is a unique piece made individually for everyone and it cannot 
be copied. The new members design the chain and create their necklaces at the welcoming/ 
introduction ceremony. After that, they can use the necklace for accessing personal data about 
themselves in the system, for example, if they want to check their contribution, they can do so in the 
Transparency Room. Since everyone wears it, it is a token uniting everyone - which can help to build 
the connection between members.  
 
Image 17: The connection medallion and console 
==PAGE:98==
 
98 
 
The chip built within the medallion has one’s personal information in it, so peers can exchange contacts 
when they meet someone. Instead of using their phone, they can simply connect with their medallion. 
All the connections made will be synced and downloaded on one’s phone - Heterotopia will probably 
have an app in the future for the most efficient information flow. This exchange of information is done 
by holding the necklaces as close to each other as illustrated above.  
These is another function of the medallion which is meant to carry special importance. It is called the 
meaningful connection. With a meaningful connection we mark a deeply personal experience that gives 
one lot of value. It can be a deep conversation or receiving help from someone which created a 
meaningful moment. When two or more Heterotopians have a so-called mutual meaningful 
connection, there is a ritual we would like to create using the medallions. As it is illustrated below the 
deep connection of the medallions turn into a gesture and will create a habit. We want this function 
to have special importance so the number of meaningful connections you can have is limited.  
The difference between the connection and the deep connection is the following. The first one is 
practical and casual and can be done as frequently as possible. The deep one, on the other hand, is 
meant to be ritualized and scarce, only working 3 times a month. This is to increase the perceived value 
of the experience, making the users more mindful of with whom they choose to do this interaction. 
See further features of the necklace in the next chapter (user scenario) Supportive Technology. 
 
==PAGE:99==
 
99 
 
5.3.4 The Welcoming Ceremony  
We designed this part to serve as a mindful welcoming to the community. The focus was on making it 
easier for new members to learn about the culture of Heterotopia.  
The introduction happens in two parts: The practical information part that happens in the daytime 
before participating in anything, and the introduction/integration part where they are in the actual 
space (Heterotopia) while it is in use by its members. In this way, the most important foundational 
information is delivered in a calm, safe and relaxed environment, where there are space and room for 
the newcomers to ask questions.  
The week before the ceremony 
On the week before the ceremony, all new members are required to participate in the introductory 
crash course in “How to be a Heterotopian”. Here they are given their personal connection medallion 
necklace piece that they are going to customize together. While decorating and creating the string of 
the necklace together, they are educated in the rules and explained about the history, principles, 
philosophy, and purpose of the place. The principles are what everyone is encouraged to follow inside 
for good culture's sake. The goal is for this to work as a preventative measure aiming to reduce any 
uncertainty and eventual anxiety that could arise from entering a new environment. It is desired that 
the new members feel as welcome, comfortable, and safe about the place before even entering so 
that they are in a way more “open” when they enter. Moreover, as it is desired that all members’ - old 
and new – interactions and experiences with themselves and others are as good as they can be at any 
given time, we see the importance of being aligned in mindset. The goal is to motivate everyone to be 
mindful and onboard with certain values like respect, care, support and encouragement from the very 
beginning. 
 
On the day of the ceremony: 
As the newcomers arrive on their first day, they are greeted by their assigned buddies, people 
specialized in welcoming those from the outside world. The buddy system is in place to aid the 
members in getting introduced, involved, understanding and maintaining the culture. 2-3 new 
members will get a buddy who will act as their main contact person and integrator to the community. 
There is a speech, which is followed by the newcomers being guided through the enTrance tunnel 
(further explanation in Touchpoint_05), where they are all greeted with big visualizations stating: 
“Welcome to Heterotopia!”. As they enter the main hall, they are met by the sight of all the existing 
members using the space and interacting with each other. As the newcomers are shown around the 
facilities and explained how to use them, their buddy introduces them to some of their friends, to 
initiate the first feeling of becoming connected to the people of the place. The buddy and his/her/their 
novice members can go on adventures and events together to follow up on different activities and help 
them with the right behavior. When this final phase is over, the newcomers are free to go where they 
desire. 
 
The welcoming and the integration is the most important touchpoint which means the buddies have 
to be carefully selected. Based on our personal experience when the integration is facilitated by an 
older, experienced member you get a more mindful introduction. All buddies should receive a training 
and newly integrated members should rate them. This fosters feedback mechanisms on the 
thoughtfulness of the buddy.  
==PAGE:100==
 
100 
 
 
5.3.5 The enTrance  
We designed a meaningful and grasping entrance for Heterotopia. Most of the time the entrance is 
just a door when you enter a place. However, for our vision it is the most important place. The entrance 
is the mechanism to help the guests to transition from the outside world to the inside world. Venues 
usually do not do this, so in our opinion the guests never have a meaningful transition. We want to 
enable every guest to set their mood and expectations while entering Heterotopia. When they do this, 
they mentally prepare themselves to enter the place. They go through a change in mood, and they 
change their behavior to one which they find comfortable, safe, and acceptable. What one feels safe 
or acceptable is different from people to people. Someone can quickly feel like they are home and be 
comfortable anywhere while for others it can take a while. We designed an entrance which facilitates 
this behavioral change. It aims to help everyone to transition into a state which helps to leave the 
outside world behind – and enter Heterotopia with an easy mind.  
 
Idea in: We discovered people might be concerned about their safety or they have some anxiety before 
they enter. We want to remove this and make them feel safe and welcomed. The enTrance tunnel) is 
connecting the Changing Room to the rest of the place. The tunnel has huge pavement blocks with 
words written on them – or screens acting as blocks where text can appear (as shown on the picture 
above). These blocks with the text shine up in front of the people as they are walking through the 
==PAGE:101==
 
101 
 
tunnel. The text is a message which can be read together word by word, forming a sentence to 
motivate and give one encouragement.  
 
Idea with: It helps to overcome one’s anxiety and adds a feeling of safety and comfort. It is an entrance 
where one can have a moment of reflection. The message that the passage shows is a nice element 
which adds to the experience of walking into the club – also making the entry different and exciting to 
look forward to. This way we wanted to make the entrance meaningful, ritualized, and uplifting. The 
features of the enTrance fulfil our desire to make the entering to an experience and facilitate the 
transitioning. It is a personalized experience for every member. It will help to set the tone and mood 
of each participant and make them feel safe and welcomed.  
 
 
 
==PAGE:102==
 
102 
 
It a space for meeting with friends or engaging in random collaborations. 
It is a catalyzer of events and an endless source of inspiration. 
5.3.6 The Main Hall & Event Horizon  
The idea with: After the entrance tunnel everyone arrives to the Main Hall which is in the middle of 
Heterotopia. It is the central gathering space for everyone. It is here where most of the major events 
take place due to its massive size. The main qualities we wanted to create is atmospheric and curiosity 
awakening. It is grounding and welcoming to enter and see the tremendous open space in front of you.   
The intention is to create a stimulating environment where anything can happen given the freedom of 
use but keeping safety in mind. Thus, it is interactive, highly customizable, and creative. This resonates 
with what $teven Ra$pa (Burning Man Associate Director) calls “permanent flexible spaces”. He draws 
inspiration from Burning Man’s unregistered Theme Camps and walk-up art projects, which would give 
place for the unexpected. He encourages future urban planners to implement this concept to 
encourage cultural vitality and flexibility. 
The idea in: A massive open space creating a solemn atmosphere. There is a huge window located on 
the far end of the room where the natural sunlight enters the warehouse and creates a feeling of high 
importance. The same mechanism which was used in gothic churches with huge rose windows to 
illuminate the space.  
The workshops and atelier spaces are located on the sides of the main hall. In the design, it was 
important to allow everyone to observe what is happening to give them ease. Because of this one 
always has a perfect overview of what is happening around him/her/them. The place has a lot of 
nature-inspired elements as they are shown in the visualization. Plants hanging from the ceiling and 
from the edges of each floor. In the middle of the Hall there is a giant head-shaped mirror ball reflecting 
the rays of the sunlight. 
==PAGE:103==
 
103 
 
 
Figure 24: Floor plan of the ground floor with the Jungle room 
 
Figure 24 is a visualization of the floor plan with the different rooms for diverse activities. It shows the 
approximate location of the different areas it also represents most of the main activities of 
Heterotopia. The central area is the Main Hall, used as hangout space, a place for communal eating, 
or a concert hall for larger events. In the middle in front of the bay window The Event Horizon takes 
place. It is the meeting point of Heterotopians which they usually use for celebration, music, and 
dancing. It is here the biggest events take place. There is also an Art Arena in the Main Hall. It is an 
ever-changing exhibition space where collaborative events can sprout and happen any time. It features 
installations made by the Heterotopians like “the Fear Cave”, a small room embodying a fear 
anonymously collected by the artist, changing every month.  
 
 
==PAGE:104==
 
104 
 
5.3.7 The Lounge  
The lounge Lounge area is one of the chill areas of Heterotopia. In the Lounge area, tables are small, 
so people can talk to everyone around it without having to raise the voice. Nuances in the tone can be 
perceived, facilitating better conversations. People are at a personal distance, and the atmosphere 
becomes less formal (Gehl, 2010). It is a comfortable place for hanging out, getting to know new 
people, or meeting up with friends. The place desires to provide a safe and social space to 
Heterotopians. It is a calm yet dynamic interaction which acts stimulatingly on anyone. We want to 
create a higher chance for random discourses where people can conflict with their values and ideas 
and learn pro-social behavior. We want to create less mobile phone use and more real-life interactions. 
Idea with: A homey environment with comfortable furniture e.g.: the couches and sofas combined 
with comfortable carpets to lay on and pillows that provide the ability to customize comfort. To help 
overcome one’s anxiety and insecurities the interior design is playing with objects familiar to everyone. 
It is not a shocking environment; it is designed to be able to feel at home rather than at a club. The 
appeal is playful and awakens curiosity. Everything is physical here, there is no digital technology, 
screens, or anything distractive. The place is informal and allows people to freely customize the 
environment and create a new order of furniture. It is a place to recharge and spend leisure time alone 
or with friends. The overall experience is a very diverse set of interactions, but it gives people some 
feeling of togetherness and presence. Increasing the number of random encounters, the chances of 
having a meaningful interaction is up to the people in the conversation. The interactions become 
meaningful and sincere in this honest and transparent space. 
==PAGE:105==
 
105 
 
Idea in: The Lounge area is elevated from the ground floor, so people step into action when they enter. 
The space spreads out on 2 floors with different types of comforting devices like hammocks and 
armchairs or a giant net floor (as visible on the visualization). Every floor has a fence as safety and 
different stairs to go up and down. People at the Lounge have a good overview of what is going around 
in the Main Hall as these are located next to each other. It is a good location for observation and 
relaxation until one find something interesting to be involved in. Instead of single seats, the lounge is 
furnished with couches and sofas where more than one person can sit at a time. Some of these couches 
are organized around a low table for better and less formal interaction. The pillows around the space 
make people engage with each other more as they can ask to borrow them. There are plants used as 
atmospheric elements and separating some parts of the lounge from others. People have a good 
overview of what is happening around them. The living room feeling creates the feeling of safety and 
helps people to lover their alert state looking for “danger”.  
Because of this, this room is also where an important element of Heterotopia’s inclusivity can be 
accessed. In order to not deter those who want to become members but do not yet have a strong 
command of the English language, there will also be a regular English-language learning opportunity, 
staffed by volunteer members of Heterotopia. In this way, membership expansion can be further 
achieved and members’ anxiety about not being able to communicate well can be assisted.    
 
 
==PAGE:106==
 
106 
 
 
==PAGE:107==
 
107 
 
5.3.8 The Jungle Room  
 
We spend most of our existence surrounded by nature but unfortunately, we lost touch with nature 
over the last few decades of human history. A sudden and drastic industrial revolution and the 
consequences that followed made us migrate to ever expanding cities, eventually separating us more 
and more from nature. The idea is that people can experience reconnection with nature because the 
environment is inspired by it.   
As an antidote to being constantly surrounded by technology in our everyday life, lacking nature, the 
Jungle Room focuses on biophilic design, “an innovative approach that emphasizes the necessity of 
maintaining, enhancing, and restoring the beneficial experience of nature in the built environment” 
(Kellert et al., 2011). It offers an experience leaving technology behind, bringing the individual closer 
to nature, into an environment that seems out of this world. By day it is an experience close to the 
ordinary, in an extraordinary social space where one is surrounded by a dense and biodiverse 
environment, with a lot of light shining through the glass roof. There are big trees all around and 
massive hanging plants/gardens from the ceiling, comfortably diverse furniture and hammocks in the 
air and on the ground, all adding to an atmosphere, intractability, and healthy indoor climate. An 
example is the “The moss pit”, designed to create spaces for socializing (where pits are close to each 
other) and places for disconnecting (where pits are far from each other). It resembles nature but in is 
clean way that is always comfortable to be in.  
At night, the environment changes. The hybrid of nature and otherworldliness becomes more evident, 
where the individual is transported into an imaginary-like world, where parts of the environment like 
grass and plants starts to glow, bringing a magical feeling of how alive nature truly is. Using new gene-
technology, most plants are here capable of self-sustained luminescence (Mitiouchkina et al., 2020). 
With a softly glowing ceiling, the artificial and natural light in the room area is brought together, 
smoothing the gap between the natural nature and the unnatural, glowing, and technological 
environment in the rest of the space.   
As nature and plants has a well-documented improving effect on both the psychological and cognitive 
well-being and the overall quality of life of individuals (Hall & Knuth, 2019), the Jungle Room is meant 
to provide a meaningful environment and a desire for more nature in our everyday life. 
The Jungle Room is an addition to the main warehouse used for Heterotopia. The area was fenced off 
and terraformed to suit the atmosphere and the experience we are intended to give. Holes and pits 
were made and well as “the moss pit” was carefully shaped out of soil. The plants and trees were 
selected for making the environment diverse and compatible. Then they were planted with an 
underground watering system integrated in the soil.  
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:108==
 
108 
 
5.3.9 Atelier and Workshop spaces 
 
The Atelier is located next to the Main Hall on the ground floor. The entrance is big and atmospheric, 
ideally a huge grass wall with a glass door in it.  The interior has a high ceiling going across the next 
floors of the structure as studies have shown that it favors creative thinking (Rui & Zhu, 2007). 
Master-apprentice system 
It is the main artistic hub of Heterotopia, the cultural center for creativity and self-expression through 
fine arts – a space every Heterotopian can use. As mentioned in the application procedure, when 
applying, it is asked what one wants to teach and what one wants to learn from others. This 
information is further used as a part of a digital framework, offering a master-apprentice system that 
is easy to access and use (via ex. the phone), which in turn is making it more accessible for people 
within Heterotopia with mutual interests to connect. Seeing the creative process and the exchange of 
knowledge will make both the teacher and the student grow, further fueled by the positive and open-
minded environment.  
The Atelier exposes the artistic process; not only the successful ones but also the failures as it is a 
natural part of the artistic process, but rarely seen. The artworks made by the members of Heterotopia 
can/will be exhibited inside the space thus creating more value and involvement of the co-created 
space. In return, it turns the environment into a motivating and inspiring atmosphere, which is both 
encouraging and genuine.  
The Workshop spaces are next to the Atelier and its accessible from the Main Hall too. It is meant for 
making DIY things and also fixing and improving the environment of Heterotopia. The space is only 
open during the day from 9-16. There are machines which can be used for manufacturing wood and 
metal as well as 3D printing and sewing machines. There is also a room just for electricals. The 
workshop is used for building things in-house on demand by the skilled members of the community. 
Because of safety and sufficient usage these machines have limited accessibility for the Heterotopians. 
However, everyone can get for access to use them but only under the supervision of a relevant 
member.  
Our vision is to help anyone to learn practical skills or to create projects on their own which can later 
grow into bigger projects backed by other members. The system works as an in-house innovation hub 
and maker space. The Workshop and the Atelier have their own rules for mindful and safe usage. The 
materials are not provided by Heterotopia as an organization, because everyone is using their own 
material. However, there is a storage space for different materials where people can bring and store 
these extra materials.  
 
 
==PAGE:109==
 
109 
 
5.3.10 Disconnection Rooms  
 
As most parts of Heterotopia are filled with different levels of sound, we also found it natural to give 
the place some balance. A place to retreat or take a break seemed not just desired, but necessary, 
especially if participants at any point find an activity too overwhelming or they simply want a break to 
gather some energy. This is the purpose the disconnection rooms serve, with different sized rooms 
providing different levels of disconnection. All the rooms are soft, filled with pillows and drapery, with 
a circular and open layout, so everyone can see everyone, giving a feeling of safety and comfort.  
Before entering any of these rooms, there is a sign encouraging the user to be mindful of others, to 
not use their phone and to enjoy the experience. If it’s for the individual, private or for groups, there 
are rooms providing the appropriate space for relaxation, meditation or sleeping. Some rooms have 
relaxing music, while others are completely soundproof and silent. Some are filled with calm lights; 
others are dark with a beautiful artificial starry sky in the ceiling. Whatever the case might be, as there 
is no desire for the experiences to interfere with each other, there will be an “sound lock” in-between 
these spaces and the sound filled spaces. A sound lock (Foley, 2013) is providing the same function for 
sound, as an airlock does for space, meaning two sound- isolated doors between the entrance and the 
space. These disconnection rooms will at the same time provide the space where different levels of 
guided events can be held by volunteering participants or booked professional facilitators.  
  
  
 
==PAGE:110==
 
110 
 
5.3.11 The Rave Cave  
 
As we explained it the literature review, studies have shown that music engagement supports the 
mental and psychological well-being of people, but with the condition that the context suit specific 
individual needs. In addition to dancing events at the Event Horizon, and in the Movement Space, the 
Heterotopians have access to the Rave Cave, providing a different context. The Rave Cave is meant to 
be a highly stimulating space where its participants are dancing joyfully together in an all-immersive 
audiovisual experience. The room provides all forms of light and audio equipment, giving developing 
and professional artists the ability to perform. Loud does not have to be unsafe, which is why all 
members are encouraged to buy each of their own high-quality sound filters available by the entrance. 
An obvious sign shows the evening's decibel levels at entry, ensuring the participant of what kind of 
protection is required to stay safe. 
5.3.12 Bass Therapy Room  
 
The Bass Therapy Room is an experimental space, functioning like a scientific sound lab exploring the 
positive effects from music, sounds and visuals. As stated in the literature review in the section “Quality 
of life”, the evidence for music supporting mental wellbeing is extensive and many (Perkins, Mason-
bertrand, et al., 2020). 
Facilitated by artists, or experts conducting research in experimental psychology, (the psychology 
concerning “any aspect of being human that involves the mind” (Farnsworth, n.d.), the room seeks to 
facilitate positive and meaningful sound and audiovisual experiences for its participants. 
An example of an audiovisual experience: The idea is to make the mind less outward-focused and more 
inside looking, by playing soundtracks of philosophical thoughts – like the recordings of Alan Watts 
combined with music that is widely popular today. In this way of facilitation, the thought is to bring 
meaningful philosophy and mindful thinking to the participants. 
Using sound engineers and sound designers, the room is created to have the best acoustics and the 
most relaxing experience for the optimal desired effect. During the sessions, the participants are laying 
comfortably on the heavily cushioned floor as the sound waves resonates through their bodies, 
creating an immersive experience together with the visuals projected in the ceiling.  
 
Conclusion 
This is the end of the description of the touchpoints. We have described the main parts of Heterotopia. 
In the next section we introduce a narrative, that will go through in depth on the user experience. It 
explains how the life inside Heterotopia looks like. We are going to show the mechanisms and the 
touchpoints in action.  
 
 
==PAGE:111==
 
111 
 
5.4 How does Heterotopia works? 
 
In this section Heterotopia is further explained in the form of a narrative story. The following chapter 
describes the concept both from emotional and logical sides, which make the mechanisms of the 
concept more understandable. Furthermore, it makes Heterotopia more alive as well as realistic. The 
ViP method argues that the design process can never be free of emotions and there is no objective 
design process. In our design approach we were also very emotional while we were developing this 
concept for a better future. Because of this we chose the format of a cartoon to illustrate our concept 
with both logically and emotionally. 
The story takes shape as a comic book. It has a chronological structure, but it always shows a different 
aspect of the concept. The comic is supported with a narration, explaining what is not visible on the 
pictures. This way the two act together as a user scenario. The cartoon with the narration can also be 
interpreted as the emotions guiding our logical thinking. Below each user cartoon (image + narration) 
there is a short callout explaining what is happening and why. It describes the mechanism, the idea 
with and the idea in of the concept. Most of the callouts represent our research and the information 
we synthesized during the project. It has many scientific sources to support our statements, but it also 
includes the reflection of our opinion.  
Expressing our feelings freely in the cartoon helped us to overcome what logic and system thinking fail 
to communicate in emotions. We received a lot of positive feedback during the validation on the 
cartoons. Many said it was useful in understanding what the concept is about. They highly praised the 
quality and consistency of the comic, and how well it led them in understanding the concept, as Steven 
Ra$pa (one of the experts) wrote back to us: “I also love the use of drawings. They are really fun and 
delightful with consistent style.”. 
Moving forward we present the cartoon. It takes place in the future and transports the reader into 
Heterotopia, illustrating, how we are imagining it to be. It illustrates the most important touchpoints 
of the concept and the user experience. 
 
 
==PAGE:112==
 
112 
 
The need 
In the year 2031, in a middle-sized city of Northern Europe, Josh, who moved to the city 1,5 years 
ago is working remotely as a customer analysis for a drone-sharing app for private use. 
 
 
Like all employees in Scandinavia, he finishes work at 3 PM - a measure implemented in 2029 to 
give more personal time to workers. But even with more time on his hands, Josh doesn’t feel 
happier or fulfilled. He is daydreaming about becoming a painter, or at least being able to be 
creative in his free time. However, instead of painting he is usually too drained and unmotivated 
from an unfulfilling job and finds himself binge-watching series in his mindfully designed 30 square 
meter home LifeHub. (LifeHub was an architectural project made in collaboration with world-
famous interior designers launched in 2026 to tackle the housing crisis, where one could pre-order 
a customized micro-home.) 
 
When Josh finally manages to fall asleep, he is dreaming about being surrounded by people who 
appreciate him. Except for his coworkers, Josh knows very few people in his city and doesn’t really 
know any interesting places to go to. He feels lonely, sometimes anxious, and lost. 
 
Adam and Josh 
 
Adam and Josh are good friends but unfortunately, they’ve are very busy, so they haven’t been 
able to meet for a long time. Josh seems quite sad; he is feeling lost recently. It is not so surprising 
since he just moved here 1,5 years ago. Adam looks really happy and it is easy to see, and they are 
both happy to finally catch up with each other. 
 
 
 
==PAGE:113==
 
113 
 
The solution 
 
Adam feels completely the opposite of Josh. After he took a friend’s advice and quit his job, he 
started to work as a set designer for a small theatre. He was always interested in trying it out 
and finally found the courage through support. Adam recently has been spending spends his time 
in the afternoon with a group of people he recently met and quickly became good friends with. He 
has found a lot of joy and appreciation in others’ company lately and he feels grateful for having 
them in his life. 
Even if the illustration above might be rather simplified and stereotyped it accurately 
shows the internal and external conflict that an individual might struggle with. We 
all have personal interests, and we all feel the weight that society put on us. Because 
of this, we are constantly trying to fit in and find the meaning of our life in the 
framework society provides to us. Josh is unaware of how the environment 
influences his mood and feelings (context factor). From our context factors, we know 
that “More than 3 Billion humans around the planet are working. Only 40% of them 
report that they are happy at work (TED Tuesdays, n.d.)”. This is an unsettling 
number. We also know that “Confidence usually comes with a greater feeling of 
relaxation that is clearly reflected in the face, and with a greater freedom of 
movement (Greene, 2018)”. This means that your feelings are influencing your body 
language. Here we see a relation between happiness at work and how that can 
influence one’s body language.   
Word of mouth 
 
As Josh is talking about all the things he is concerned about these days, Adam feels sorry for his 
friend and he would like to help him. He has a suggestion. He has been the member of a club called 
Heterotopia for almost 6 months. He talks very highly about it and he wants to show it to Josh. 
Adam and Josh share similar values, and they are both open-minded people. 
Because of this, Adam thinks both Josh and Heterotopia would benefit from each 
other.  
==PAGE:114==
 
114 
 
Our opinion is that the quality of one’s experience is mostly influenced by the 
quality of one’s environment.  Here we are mostly concerned of about the built 
environment and the people who are in it. Following this logic, we argue that the 
quality of the place depends on the quality of the people who are there. If everyone 
is aware of this, we assume that anyone would only bring a few carefully selected 
friends to Heterotopia, people who would contribute and gain from the 
community. Because of this, the place does not need any advertising that would 
attract the crowds of people, but not necessarily the right people. The channels 
used to promote the place is mostly word of mouth. This also means natural and 
healthy growth.  
Application process 
 
Adam and Josh went to the venue to get the application paper for membership. Josh needs to fill 
it out with his personal information as well as a little bit about himself, his motivation of why he 
desires to join, how he wants to use the space, what he wishes to contribute with, what he wants 
to teach, what he wants to learn from others, and his core moral values. In return, he receives an 
identification necklace that he’ll later personalize, together with and a membership card. 
People who want to become Heterotopians must register and apply in advance. 
Anyone can apply, but the registration cannot be done at entry! This is to filter out 
undesired behavior and spontaneous guests showing up randomly while not being 
familiar with the concept. After registration, they must wait until the next 
Welcoming Ceremony, which is held twice a month on every second Saturday.  
Integration to the community 
 
The Big day arrives! Josh and the other new members are about to receive their welcoming 
ceremony. Suddenly, a funny-looking guy with a funky moustache called Steven shows up and 
welcomes them warmly. He starts by greeting them one by one. He starts his welcoming speech 
and explaining what Heterotopia is, it’s history and vision. He talks about the principles that 
everyone is encouraged to follow inside for good culture's sake. 
==PAGE:115==
 
115 
 
Inclusiveness! Integration! The shared vision of the community become the best 
when the people from the outside world are mindfully integrated and introduced 
to the community. In the Welcoming Ceremony the new members get their 
identifying objects (membership card and Connection medallion). After this, the 
new members are integrated one-by-one into the community with the help of the 
Buddies and the Principles. 
 
Our success story 
 
Heterotopia started with a few friends who wanted to create a place where they can hang out. 
They wanted to be safe and distant from the outside world because they felt it is too narrow-
minded and commercialized. They wanted a little island of joy in the city where they live, a place 
for being together. As they found ways of making this place, more people joined and shared their 
interest. Everyone contributed with something they could offer. They forged a strong community 
over shared dinners and celebrations. Attracting like-minded people, the community has expanded 
organically over the last decade, and they are now more than 300 members co-owning an old 
industrial building.  
Heterotopia is based upon a strong collective. It cannot be copied and sold as a 
franchise. It can only be scaled naturally with the designed framework and the 
mindset behind the idea. The founders of Heterotopia had a vision, so they created 
a place for it. Over the next couple of years, it grew and changed and matured into 
what it is described in the concept. The Principles were made during this time to 
maintain the vision. As Heterotopia evolved the social dynamics changed as well. 
The Principles had to evolve simultaneously to fit to the present needs. This 
illustrates how agile and modular the framework which is used to make the 
concept. The ability to change any time is fundamental to maintain the place’s 
healthiness and the refined vision. People who joined early participated in forming 
the vision they became strong core members of Heterotopia.  
 
 
==PAGE:116==
 
116 
 
The entrance 
 
After Josh receives his introduction, he meets with Adam who was waiting for him in the changing 
room. They put on their funky clothes and they are now ready to go inside. They walk together 
through the “enTrance tunnel”. On the way, Josh sees the pavement light up in front of him as a 
sort of guidance. Then he realizes there is a message on the floor. All the pavement blocks have 
one word on them, and they light up always in a different order. If you read them together you 
get a sentence. Each sentence is unique and for the person who walks on the pavement. Josh is 
reading out the words to Adam as they walk, You…. Are…. Beautiful. It makes him smile. Josh and 
Adam are wearing some interesting clothes of their liking. Adam has his usual fur vest and Josh 
brought a hat he never dared to wear before in public. 
The clothes represent our actual inner persona. Dressing according to this is a 
fundamental part of self-expression in Heterotopia. We encourage everyone to 
dress in a way that makes them feel special. It is like trying out a different version 
of yourself (persona) when you dress up. Later the validation received from others 
on our persona creates a positive feedback loop and acts as a confidence booster. 
After the members use the changing room, they go through the entrance tunnel. It 
is an ever-changing personalized experience helping one to reflect and be mindful 
in Heterotopia. 
The first impression 
 
At the end of the tunnel, Josh and Adam arrived at the main hall which is one of the leisure places 
of Heterotopia. Leisure is completely reimagined inside Heterotopia. One can choose between 
sofas, armchairs and hammocks or Moroccan type spaces with pillows and big cushions. Leisure is 
a pleasure! Josh was wonderstruck by the interior as they stepped inside. Everything was filled 
with plants, giving him the feeling of being in a rainforest, surrounded by plants growing, hanging 
everywhere. The atmosphere was calm and peaceful, with people hanging out between the trees in 
cozy areas.  
==PAGE:117==
 
117 
 
In Heterotopia people can experience a reconnection with nature because the 
environment is inspired by biophilic design. By using simple decorations and rather 
having a large diversity of plants, we want to make the users to feel grounded and 
more connected to nature.  
A Hangout Place 
 
Adam showed his favorite place to chill to Josh. They quickly engaged in a conversation with 
Ophelia. Josh was welcomed by her and received a compliment on his hat which made him proud of 
himself and more self-confident in wearing it. They got comfortable and started to chat as if it 
was the most natural thing on earth. Josh looked around and saw people around him on the floor 
and in other strange places, hanging, laying, and sitting. It looked like a place where everyone just 
enjoys being comfortable and relaxed. Josh felt a connection with Ophelia, so he started to talk 
about how much he would like to paint but he feels so unmotivated to do it alone. As it turned out, 
his new friend was a painter herself.  
The informal Lounge area provides a safe and social environment for 
Heterotopians. It is stimulating and helps people to engage in random discourses. 
It is the mindful arrangement of the furniture and the dynamics that elevates one’s 
barriers and allows greater self-expression and easier interaction. It aims to help 
one overcome anxiety, discomfort, and vulnerability. It makes socializing a 
meaningful, desireable, and important. With the chillout areas we mean to create 
presence, togetherness, and a diverse ever-changing environment.   
Personal development 
 
Josh joins Ophelia at the Atelier. The organized chaos of brushes and pigments and the smells of 
fresh painting fills Josh with joy and inspiration. Josh takes out his sketchbook from his bag and 
shows his drawings to Ophelia. He is usually insecure about showing his sketches but not when the 
stakes are so high. This is his first chance finally to engage in a conversation with an artistic mind 
in a long time. Ophelia really likes his drawing and repeats some ‘inspirational quotes’ to motivate 
him. Then she shares her philosophy about painting and creating. Josh enjoys the conversation, 
==PAGE:118==
 
118 
 
and he takes away a lot of ideas that he was keen to try out. At home, he started starts to make 
sketches and paint. Next time they meet with his friend, he shows her the painting he made after 
their brainstorming. Eventually, Ophelia offers to mentor Josh. The professional support and the 
amazing Atelier gave Josh the boost of motivation he needed to finally start actively engaging in 
his artistic pursuits. 
 
At Heterotopia we are helping people to expand their social network by designing 
the space for increasing random discourses between members. This turns into a 
good network of friends. A good network will give the members more opportunity 
to reach their goals and their self-actualization. With the support of the Principles 
and the Master-Apprentice system, we want to boost the creative potential of 
everyone. Josh is the apprentice and he got personal help from a more experienced 
person -the master- Ophelia.  
By regularly practicing painting with Ophelia, Josh could get through his creative crisis. He is 
feeling revitalized and more aligned with his ideal self. The comfortable and atmospheric chillout 
places became the favorite spots, inviting him to relax and reflect. Besides painting, he signed up 
for a psychology and sleep workshop which gives him a better insight into who he is and starts to 
work on himself.  
Learning 
 
Flower Princess and Josh are reading in the library of Heterotopia. Sometimes it’s good to 
disconnect from the vibrant bustling atmosphere and enjoy a good book. Later they attended Mr. 
Magic’s masterclass about how to have a better sleep. He is an acknowledged expert on the topic. 
They all felt shocked by some of the facts they just heard, and it made them adopt new changes 
to improve their daily life. Next week Flower Princess makes a workshop on how to pickle 
mushrooms. Adam and Josh join too; they have a lot of fun! Some events are open for the public, 
so they can get a feel of what Heterotopia is about. After having participated in a public talk by 
a marine biologist talking about plastic pollution, Josh asks the speaker how he can help. He ends 
up borrowing drones from his company to film polluted areas and thereby raising the awareness 
about the situation. In Heterotopia, many containers traditionally made of plastic are made of a 
new type of 3d-printed ceramic and are completely biodegradable 
One can find it overwhelming to keep up with this continuous information flow of 
the 21st century. Mostly because there is too much information, which is too 
diverse, and one can hardly find what is meaningful or not. However, almost 
everyone has a hobby, a field of interest where they are more specialized. We 
imagined if everyone would help each other to learn something new, it would be a 
great meaningful way of getting information. Suddenly one can access knowledge, 
they never thought about from their friends, network.  
==PAGE:119==
 
119 
 
Heterotopia’s vision is to allow people to grow personally, professionally, 
individually, and communally. The key principle to this is the encouragement to 
share your interest with others. Flower Princess and Steven use the same principle 
to share their knowledge and help others. The idea comes from the rise and success 
of MasterClass and other online educational platforms where students can access 
lectures in various fields held by experts.  
Self-expression 
 
Josh already knows that everyone likes to wear something special in Heterotopia; it is part of 
their authentic self. Josh is in the changing room putting on his bob hat. He just met with CowBoi 
who has his western boots on. He is obsessed with cowboy movies and wants to live in the romantic 
picture he has about this lifestyle. They decide to hit the dancefloor immediately – it’s always a 
good idea at Heterotopia. However, even though they like to have fun sometimes it is good to stop 
for a minute and relax. So, they decided to lay down for a little while and see the moving lights 
behind the artificial canopy of the Chillout room. 
 
Our definition of self-expression is feeling, acting, doing as one wants without any 
constrains. This resonates with one of the unspoken rules of Burning Man’s 
beginnings “one can do anything until one is not affecting negatively other people’s 
experience”! In our opinion, the easiest and most effective way to practice self-
expression is to dress like you want (explained above).  
Self-expression is also acting as you want and moving as you want. A good example 
here is dancing. It is proven dance reduces stress (Bräuninger, 2012) and has a lot 
of potential health benefits like aiding in reducing anxiety and depression. (Duberg 
et al., 2013) It is also one of the most authentic forms of self-expression as the 
movements come from the dancer’s emotions and feelings evoked by the music – 
like ecstatic dance. Ecstatic dance events in the last few years sprout and spread 
across the globe spreading a new meaning. ‘Ecstatic Dance is a form of dynamic 
meditation, whereby the music is the teacher; there is no structure or steps to 
follow, you simply move in the way your body tells you to’(D, n.d.). Self-expression 
for us is basically anything your body or mind tells you to do. If one would like to 
sit down or take a nap, one should feel comfortable to do so – assuming a safe 
environment. We want to encourage a culture where one acts more mindfully 
towards the others but still be able to realize his/her/their needs.  Which in turn 
leads to a deeper self-connection and connection with others!  
 
 
==PAGE:120==
 
120 
 
Rituals 
 
The life in Heterotopia is full of small and big events all surrounded by rituals. Josh and Flower 
Princess are on a cacao-ceremony. Josh wanted to reflect on some of his thought that kept him 
awake at night. He felt comfortable to open up about them to Flower Princess. It made him feel 
less alone with his struggle. Later the week they met again for communal dinner which is twice a 
month where everyone gathers and eats communally. After the food, they all have a comfortable 
place in the resting areas to relax and digest. At 11 pm they light a huge bone fire with a big 
celebration, music, and dancing.  
Celebrating 
 
Steven just announced that the weekend has officially started. The weekends are the most 
amazing parts of the week at Heterotopia Josh knows this by now. He is excited to dive into the 
experiences. Friday night always starts with a big feast as they enjoy preparing food together as 
well as eating it communally. Then the night unexpectedly turned into a festive celebration where 
Mr. Magic played his bass and Adam his saxophone.  
 
In general celebrations have an elevated mood and a merry atmosphere, and they 
make one’s life more meaningful. At Heterotopia one can celebrate anything at any 
time. Celebrating together helps to keep the members of Heterotopia connected 
and involves them in shared memories which can turn into meaningful rituals. 
Anything can be ritualized, small or big events equally. For example, a Coffee 
ceremony every day at 1 pm, or the Summer Solstice Festival can both be equally 
important rituals in one’s life. In our opinion the importance of rituals is closely 
linked to celebrating and they are mutually important.  
   
 
==PAGE:121==
 
121 
 
We are a family! 
 
Josh just saw Flower Princess who seemed quite troubled. He walked up to her to cheer her up. 
She was sad because she had previously had an argument with her best friend. After listening, he 
advised her to have a walk with him to the chillout room. While they were talking, Josh gave his 
best opinion about the problem, which in turn made Flower Princess see it from a different 
perspective. It helped her to approach the stressful situation with a clear new mindset. On the 
walk, they met with some of their friends and joined them on the sofa. She was grateful to have 
such good friends in her life. 
 
Heterotopia is a place for the people; it is not about the place itself. The place is 
just a framework which is filled up by the members. We consider everyone who is 
a member to be part of the same family. Collectively taking care of everyone “One 
for all, all for one!”. This means that we are all connectively connected and not just 
individually participating.  
Amazing Environment 
 
Heterotopia is full of crazy adventures and mind-blowing artistic manifestations. The Great Puffer 
is a huge Fish-shaped art car. It can make huge soap bubbles which encapsulate people. Everyone 
is queuing to get a ride. The Jungle room has hidden pleasure islands for leisure and private 
conversations. Josh really likes this spot with the hammock on the tree. It is a homey environment 
within a small artificial rainforest. The environment is always changing and brings surprises which 
make Josh go WOW all the time. The newest installation is the ice-cream tube next to the 
dancefloor.  
All of this sounds ambitious but what is really behind the scenes of Heterotopia? 
We are aiming to create an environment so distracting -in a positive way- that the 
members are always able to find something according to their desires. We create 
an environment full of entertaining and carefully designed stimulations. All of this 
makes everyone participating in the ocean of events. Having diverse environments 
==PAGE:122==
 
122 
 
of intensity our intention is to make people less interested in what is happening in 
the outside world - so they use their phones less often. This would allow a greater 
‘flow’ and an atmosphere where everyone is mindfully present. 
The Moss Pit 
 
Josh’s favorite place is the Moss Pit. The Moss Pit is a place to feel connected to nature. It always 
calms Josh when he feels like lacking some energy. The moss pit is a giant sunken sofa with a moss-
like texture, with small pits unevenly distributed across it- and he lays down in a hollow with a view 
of other people hanging out. The Moss Pit is designed to create spaces for socializing (where pits 
are close to each other) and places for disconnecting (where pits are far from each other). He 
likes to look at the small artificial stars that shine above his head. In the evening, the grass in 
this pit starts to glow. Slowly, people naturally gather around these pits of light and Josh finds 
himself surrounded by unfamiliar yet friendly faces. The soothing and reassuring atmosphere 
makes Josh feel relaxed and present, and while conversing he finally feels connected to other 
people. 
 
Supportive Technology 
 
Josh just wanted to Shazam a song and accidentally winded up on social media. There is no problem 
with that as long as it does not ruin others experience. Luckily, a sensor built in his necklace is 
activated from the light emitted from his phone. After 3 minutes the sensor starts to emit a 
blinking red light from the crystal of the necklace. This light then turns into a fast-flashing strobe 
at this point it starts to annoy people around Josh, while reminding Josh that he should be present, 
so he puts his phone away. It gives him an idea to make an IoT bracelet with IFTTT so he can 
Shazam songs by pressing the button on his bracelet. This way he can stay in flow and stay 
connected. This idea eventually turned into the “Shazam Bracelet” - his idea, that was 
crowdfunded and developed within 3 months, and is now produced on demand inside of Heterotopia. 
He enjoyed working with mechatronics, which made him switch position in his company to a more 
technical-oriented position. 
 
==PAGE:123==
 
123 
 
We discovered in the context factors that the future will be even more distractive 
with the technological gadgets we are surrounding ourselves with. We cannot 
influence global trends, but we can think about how to turn technology to our 
advantage. Technology is the biggest advantage of our lifetime and we must use it 
wisely in our favor. At Heterotopia we want to build the environment with 
supportive technology - to connect us instead of disconnecting. Our main concern 
is smartphones and how can we diminish their usage. One example is Josh’s 
necklace which makes Josh use his phone less often because of the disturbing light 
it emits, and it is annoying for him and other people too.  
Another idea is an RFID signal blocking pouch for phones. The advantage of this is 
that participants do not have to change anything in the settings of their phone to 
get disconnected they just simply have to put the phones in the pouch, and it stops 
receiving notifications. When taking out and use their phones it automatically 
connects to the network again and they see if they have missed anything 
important. In our workshop space, we want to provide professional help (with 
members) and equipment to make such technological inventions as the Shazam 
bracelet. If the project proved to be useful such an accessory can be founded by 
the people who are interested in using it.  
Bass Therapy 
 
Our friends are in the Bass Therapy room. They are about to get a therapeutic session with the 
guidance of Mr. Magic. Bass Therapy is Mr Magic’s invention; he wrote his PhD about the Healing 
effects of the low-frequency bass waves. He is now using a combination of bass sounds and a 
guided meditation. He is facilitating a journey where Josh, Adam and Flower Princess are learning 
about their emotions. Josh experiences some anxiety, and he wants to make peace with it. The 
experience starts with an increasing frequency of bass waves then Mr. Magic guides a breathing 
exercise which helps them into deep meditation mode. Then he is talking about how to approach 
their emotions in the everyday life rationally.  
 
The Bass Therapy is part of the experimental events at Heterotopia where the 
sound is used to help one to relax, disconnect or get into a meditative state. As 
research has shown, music has great potential as a tool for increased mental 
wellbeing (Perkins, Mason-Bertrand, et al., 2020). Developed with a strong 
foundation in science, we hope that the Bass Therapy room can both contribute 
positively internally to its members, and to its exterior with open-source research. 
 
==PAGE:124==
 
124 
 
Dream Circle 
 
Josh recently joined the Dream Circle and has since then started to write in his dream diary every 
day from the moment he wakes up. Then on Thursdays, they gather in a circle within Heterotopia, 
taking turns where everyone shares their dreams from the past week. In the beginning, Josh could 
not remember anything from his dream but now he got used to writing them down which also had 
an impact on his dreams. He is so excited to tell the others about the adventures he had with a 
friendly dolphin who he was flying with the other night. Everyone enjoyed his story, especially the 
part when they escaped from the giant’s castle on a rainbow slide. The best part of the dream 
circle is that everyone can openly talk about how crazy things they dream about each night, and 
they can laugh about it together. They are just dreams after all. Or are they? 
 
The idea of the Dream Circle came from a real experience and its purpose is to 
practice mindful dreaming. Everyone likes to listen to stories and our dreams are 
always fascinating creations of our unconscious mind, and “reverse engineering” 
them together can be a lot of fun. So, the dream circle is a great place to practice 
dreaming, as “dream recall is underestimated by retrospective measures and 
enhanced by logbooks” (Aspy, 2016). Also, the event acts as a steppingstone where 
everyone can entertain each other and listen and learn the arts of storytelling. 
 
==PAGE:125==
 
125 
 
  
 
==PAGE:126==
 
126 
 
Five months later Josh feels more confident and more in touch with himself. He is now surrounded 
by a community supporting him in his interests, most importantly in his artistic pursuits. New 
friends! Josh feels a strong sense of belongingness in this community that collectively takes care 
of everyone. He has gradually replaced his time online at home, with hanging out and engaging in 
collective activities with his friends. He enjoys participating in Heterotopia’s rituals, such as the 
early Monday Morning Party and the frequently held big communal dinners, where people are 
encouraged to cook food from their own culture and share it. Initially introduced by his friend to 
Heterotopia, he is now himself inviting people he thinks would benefit, just in the same way he did. 
 
In the future, there will be several Heterotopias in a city and all around the world, 
following the same concept. Current members are encouraged to start or help to 
start up the same concept in a new location. Expanding this way guarantees that 
the offspring stay true to the vision. The knowledge generated inside Heterotopias 
will be accessible for everyone on an open-source peer-reviewed online library, 
beneficiating society for the greater good. 
 
 
Conclusion 
 
This narrative presented the user experience through the eyes of a persona called Josh – a new 
member of Heterotopia. The interaction with the different elements was shown and the atmosphere 
what we want to make people feel – connectively connected. The next chapter is about the validation 
and evaluation of our design intervention. 
 
==PAGE:127==
 
127 
 
 
Chapter 6:  
Evaluation of the Concept 
==PAGE:128==
 
128 
 
In this chapter we will detail our evaluation process, present the results and what changes we made to 
our concept. As social designer, we focused on assessing the social relevance of the project. We 
proceeded to an internal evaluation rated our project based on the UN Sustainable Development Goals 
(SDGs). We also reached out to domain experts and conducted a narrative-based study, a method 
suited for assessing social impact early on in a project, described by Tromp & Hekkert in Designing for 
Society (Tromp & Hekkert, 2018). 
6.1 Narrative-based study 
 
Approach 
Early evaluation of the design proposal when designing innovative solutions. When designing for social 
impact, assessment is especially important. It is important to address following questions: How likely 
is it that the design intervention lead to the intended behavioral change? and How likely is it that it will 
lead to the desired social implication? It is also a good occasion to collect insights from domain experts 
on what elements or good, and which can be improved.  
The social relevance was assessed by a Narrative-based study, an evaluation method described in 
Designing for Society (Tromp & Hekkert, 2018).  A short narrative accompanied by illustrations, follows 
a character with goals and intentions using the design intervention and describes any consequences. 
The story follows a narrative arc: first the context is described (in our case, the life and associated 
issues of an urbanite in 2031) – he is then introduced to Heterotopia, and the story tell how the use of 
the place leads to specific, pro-social behaviors. 
Domain experts composed mainly of alternative and transformative event makers, as well as 
sociologists, were set to assess the social relevance. They were sent a short narrative and a survey. For 
each six intended behavioral change, they had to answer whether it will be initiated by using 
Heterotopia. The same was asked for each intended social implication. To collect insights, feedback 
and ideas for improvement, and they were asked to elaborate why for each question.  
The narrative-based study presented several advantages for us. Firstly, our experts being spread across 
many countries (from Norway to the United States), a virtual prototype was more appropriate than a 
physical one. Secondly, because of the COVID-19 crisis, it was impossible to conduct any experiment. 
Finally, the narrative-based study induces transportation – an efficient way to absorb the reader in the 
created future context. 
The narrative and the survey can be found in Appendix F. 
6 female and 7 male experts gave us feedback. It is worth noting that what they were asked for 
feedback on what was a short narrative story from before the concept was finished. Some of the 
aspects of the concepts have been refined based on the feedback we received. 
  
 
 
==PAGE:129==
 
129 
 
The 13 people who came back had the following occupations: 
 
Researcher 
 
Retired university professor 
 
Economist 
 
Special consultant 
 
Culture Developer

Entrepreneur 
 
Community Development 
and Event Production for an 
arts non-profit
