H: Reflection 
H.1: Reflection on the steps of the ViP process and SID 
Limits of SID 
• 
Focused on only 1 social implication! 
Domain 
• 
Our idea for this project was still unclear at this phase because we haven’t had a company to 
work with who would give us a clear domain. Therefore, the domain was hard to find because 
we saw many sides of the same coin equally important.  
Generation of Context Factors 
• 
The generation of context factors was very diverging and lengthy. We took inspiration from 
many different topics but with an unclear focus, so we had numerous context factors where 
most of it was too shallow and not so interesting to work with at the end 
Clustering the context factors: 
- 
This task is the most important and time-consuming step of the ViP process (Hekkert & Van 
Dijk, 2011). Because of the too many context factors we have generated we had to analyse 
almost 500 of these. Organizing these context factors was a big task and we used lot of time 
on discussing them and trying to find the emerging quality between the clusters. Instead of 
tring and failing as the method suggest we spent too much time with organizing and debating 
about them. At the end all of us had a different approach so we allowed ourselves to 
individually try out different things. When we presented our findings to each other helped 
shaping the future context however it was not this what made the breakthrough. The method 
argues for the unconscious processing power of the brain which is best at problem solving. 
However, this takes time but then the future context emerged just as the method said it will. 
Statement 
- 
In a group of 3 it is really important everyone has the same understanding which needs 
discussion, understanding and paying attention to the language and alignment of the mindset. 
- 
It is not always so clear how to use the VIP design guide, so we had many conflicting 
interpretations on how freely can we use it. 
Interaction qualities 
- 
It was unclear how many of these should we have since our ambitions and the concept seemed 
big even after the statement definition. 
- 
Hard when the understanding of the word is different than the meaning the dictionary says. 
We had to define our new meaning at the end. 
- 
Hard to find the right words as not native English speaking 
==PAGE:220==
 
220 
 
Product qualities 
- 
We made numerous product qualities what needed also additional explanation and 
organization 
- 
At this step we had very concrete ideas about the concept which we could not let out because 
the process did not allow us to do so. This pile of ideas influenced our rational decision making. 
Concepting & Detailing 
- 
As our concept was truly innovative but in combining different ideas into a novel concept it 
was hard to see its relevance in the beginning and communicating. 
- 
It was hard to combine other models or methods to VIP.  
The concept was too ambitious and concept to be detailed out in all mechanisms, because of this we 
needed 3 weeks of extension for the project. 
H.2: Reflection of the process 
Team member roles 
- 
Starting off the project we agreed in an honest and transparent communication flow to ease 
to process. Since we are three close friends, we had to make rules for this new type of 
interaction between us.  
- 
Similar strength and weaknesses (amplifying both), made it hard for certain tasks while others 
were overdone 
- 
Once team roles based on our unique strengths were decided, productivity suddenly rose 
- 
However, understanding each other is not always easy if none of us in native English speaker. 
This turned out to be one of the biggest challenges in our project when we faced with 
describing and understanding abstract ideas. 
- 
All the three of us is different and we had different needs which challenged our efficiency and 
friendship. 
Vision alignment 
- 
Before and throughout the project we set our vision, expectations, and wishes about what do 
we want multiple times.  
- 
Understanding our differences and similarities was important to identify our strength and 
weaknesses. This made us more aligned in vision, stronger as a project team, and eventually 
more compatible for the project.  
Time Management 
- 
Lot of time used for creating the statement and condensing the vast amount of context factors 
- 
We lost most of the time in communication whether it was internal (between us, we had or 
external (trying to reach out to others for different reasons) 
- 
Not enough time for concepting (extension needed) 
 
==PAGE:221==
 
221 
 
Research 
- 
Very broad in a lot of different domains (History, Design, Psychology, Human behavior, 
Urbanisation etc. Really good to research, since we all chose topics that passionate us. Good 
references 
- 
Made it harder to narrow down later and decide on the domain (double-edged sword) 
Interviews 
- 
Very good use of our network 
- 
Unique insights in how to make impactful transformative events 
- 
Maybe a bit too many Burning-man related organisers among the interviewees – but at that 
stage it was hard to know what else would be relevant (because we were in the part of the 
process where we were still generating context factors). Maybe half of interviews should have 
been chosen and interviewed after building the context. 
- 
Some important people took a long time to reach out too 
- 
Everyone super interested in our project (and willing to help)! 
Design process 
- 
We had a lot of abstract ideas and all of us is better in diverging than converging so we had to 
deal with a lot of data at any time 
- 
Lot of time spent with discussing abstract topics when the ViP method was not clear on how 
to make decisions 
- 
Creating something was always easier than finding ways to document it regularly, because of 
this our idea generation process was hard to follow in the aftermath 
Collaborations 
- 
Very difficult because of COVID-19 
- 
Difficult to start collaborations on the way because of the nature of VIP – not being able to 
explain how the concept will materialize until the very end 
- 
We received a lot of interest towards our project but eventually due to the situation and the 
lengthiness of the communication we couldn’t find a collaboration partner 
Benchmarking 
- 
Hard to integrate in VIP, because the domain is less obvious and less specific. Very 
heterogenous group, hard to compare so different things 
- 
Usually, benchmarking is done in the beginning of a project. We decided to conduct it later in 
the the design process, in parrelel to step 7: Concepting. There are reasons for this unusual 
scheduling. First, because doing it before would only make it less focused.  
- 
Helped us become more concrete, by looking at existing places 
- 
Was an important “innovativity check”
